        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715136153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4382133366024356373"><b>*4.5 Racing Stars* </b><br/><br/>Before I started reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17798287.Driven__The_Driven_Trilogy___1_' title='Driven (The Driven Trilogy, #1) by K. Bromberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Driven</a> I had heard people comparing it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_' title='Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fifty Shades of Grey</a>. I can see some similarities but to me it felt more like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13572249.Bared_to_You__Crossfire___1_' title='Bared to You (Crossfire, #1) by Sylvia Day' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bared to You</a>. There were some cheesy lines like: <i>"Me playing Ana to his Christian." </i>Either way this book holds its own in entertaining the readers. <br/><br/><b>Colton</b> is the bad boy with a sordid past. He's a famous racecar driver who has commitment issues. <b>Reylee</b> is the 'do-gooder' with a tragic past. These two are drawn to each other even thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText4382133366024356373" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Racing Stars* </b><br><br>Before I started reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17798287.Driven__The_Driven_Trilogy___1_" title="Driven (The Driven Trilogy, #1) by K. Bromberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Driven</a> I had heard people comparing it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_" title="Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James" rel="nofollow noopener">Fifty Shades of Grey</a>. I can see some similarities but to me it felt more like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13572249.Bared_to_You__Crossfire___1_" title="Bared to You (Crossfire, #1) by Sylvia Day" rel="nofollow noopener">Bared to You</a>. There were some cheesy lines like: <i>"Me playing Ana to his Christian." </i>Either way this book holds its own in entertaining the readers. <br><br><b>Colton</b> is the bad boy with a sordid past. He's a famous racecar driver who has commitment issues. <b>Reylee</b> is the 'do-gooder' with a tragic past. These two are drawn to each other even though they feel like they are all wrong for one another. <br><br>This is the third book this week that I've read that has a major cliffhanger and the series isn't complete. I think I'm glutton for punishment.<br><br><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17798287.Driven__The_Driven_Trilogy___1_" title="Driven (The Driven Trilogy, #1) by K. Bromberg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1366000080s/17798287.jpg" alt="Driven (The Driven Trilogy, #1) by K. Bromberg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17880708.Fueled__The_Driven_Trilogy___2_" title="Fueled (The Driven Trilogy, #2) by K. Bromberg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1375489908s/17880708.jpg" alt="Fueled (The Driven Trilogy, #2) by K. Bromberg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17880714.Crashed__The_Driven_Trilogy___3_" title="Crashed (The Driven Trilogy, #3) by K. Bromberg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1369956159s/17880714.jpg" alt="Crashed (The Driven Trilogy, #3) by K. Bromberg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Cliffhangers<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4382133366024356373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1618268703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618268703" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618268703?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=life-s-too-fucking-short">life-s-too-fucking-short</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=porn-on-the-cob">porn-on-the-cob</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kindle-freebie-graveyard">kindle-freebie-graveyard</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618268703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16596918025406171767"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/><b>DNF @ 5%</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>My friends' reviews for this book are actually pretty terrifying. There's a whole line of one-star DNF reviews, which is why I think I've owned this book for years without touching it. I must have gotten it for free from the Kindle store because this isn't the type of book I'd buy. It's one of those FIFTY SHADES OF GREY knock-offs that were so popular in the wake of FSoG's blistering popularity, where people were scrambling to fi</span>
  <span id="freeText16596918025406171767" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br><b>DNF @ 5%</b><br><br><br><br>My friends' reviews for this book are actually pretty terrifying. There's a whole line of one-star DNF reviews, which is why I think I've owned this book for years without touching it. I must have gotten it for free from the Kindle store because this isn't the type of book I'd buy. It's one of those FIFTY SHADES OF GREY knock-offs that were so popular in the wake of FSoG's blistering popularity, where people were scrambling to find new ways to write the authoritarian man/doormat naif trope and make it "hott."<br><br><b> </b><br><br>The book opens with our dunce heroine marveling at her ability to remember things (no, seriously) and fretting about her organza dress and heels, when she hears people in a supply closet doing things that definitely don't sound like inventorying (I mean, unless inventory is your passion-- I'm sure someone out there goes "OH GOD" and "YES" while checking the database, and I am equally certain that this person is probably not very popular at parties).<br><br><br><br>Anyway, the heroine judges this unseen and vocal inventorist, thinking smugly "I wouldn't do that if you paid me." Which is kind of true, because not five pages later, she does it for free. You know, before deciding better of it (she's not that kind of girl, you know), and thereby giving the hero a chance to show off his rapey side by saying "I don't take anything that isn't given to me so you must have been giving it to me" (because gaslighting) and going all apeshit at the idea of refusal.<br><br><br><br>From there, you just know it's going to be a hot mess of courting (i.e. stalking), relationship issues (i.e. other women and more rapeyness), and setting boundaries (i.e. cutting down on said rapeyness and turning down expensive gifts for moral reasons, i.e. not being that kind of girl). I'm not psychic, I've just read enough of these FSoG-alikes to know the typical trajectory of the plot, and while I get that that predictability makes them fun for some, for me it's like nails on a chalkboard.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>
  <a data-text-id="16596918025406171767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_630084269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630084269" />
    <a title="Mirjana **DTR - Down to Read**" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read"><img alt="Mirjana **DTR - Down to Read**" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504717217p2/3068938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630084269?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mirjana **DTR - Down to Read**" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mirjana **DTR - Down to Read**" href="/user/show/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read">Mirjana **DTR - Down to Read**</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=i-m-broken">i-m-broken</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=mo-money-mo-problems">mo-money-mo-problems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=talk-dirty-to-me">talk-dirty-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=athletes">athletes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=too-hot-for-tv">too-hot-for-tv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=paparazzi">paparazzi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630084269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456334962822808601"><br/><b>
  <i><u>UPDATE</u> - Someone recently liked my review and I came back to re-read what I wrote for this first book in one of my favorite series. I felt the need to update the review with a quick note. I have never in my MANY years of reading seen such a change/improvement from a debut book to everything else going forward from an author. It pains me that this series has such a weak start and that this first book might put people off from reading the rest of this series. <br/><br/>Because people....YOU WOULD BE SERI</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText1456334962822808601" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i><u>UPDATE</u> - Someone recently liked my review and I came back to re-read what I wrote for this first book in one of my favorite series. I felt the need to update the review with a quick note. I have never in my MANY years of reading seen such a change/improvement from a debut book to everything else going forward from an author. It pains me that this series has such a weak start and that this first book might put people off from reading the rest of this series. <br><br>Because people....YOU WOULD BE SERIOUSLY MISSING OUT!! Books 2 and 3 are fantastic. The angst, the emotion, the passion...SO DAMN GOOD! That's all I wanted to say. Carry on. </i>
</b><br><br><br><b>***3 Whiplash Stars***</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"He gets me so worked up. So angry. I can't figure out what I want to do more, punch him or fuck him."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>And that pretty much sums up this whole book. There was so much back and forth between these two that I think I hurt myself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414467041ra/11657940.gif" width="516" height="290" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A health warning should have been included: A visit to the chiropractor may be necessary upon completion. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414467041ra/11657941.gif" width="400" height="221" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, I will admit that I was warned about this first book. I was told that it starts slow, to have patience...it will all be worth it in the end. Well, now that I've finished, I'm thinking people meant the end of the series, not the end of the book. <br><br>I'm not going to go into detail about the story since most have already read this series, so I'll just give my thoughts and feelings.<br><br>I will reiterate what I've been told. This book starts off slooooooooow. In my opinion, it takes almost 40% of the book before it even begins to take off, but even after that we're coasting at residential area speeds. I understand that it's laying the foundation to the series, but come on <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390124699ra/8147076.gif" width="245" height="160" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A huge chunk of the book consisted of repetitive and circular dialogue and actions. Both characters constantly contradicting their words and actions. Too much...<br><br>I want you.<br>I'm bad for you.<br>I need you.<br>You should stay away.<br>I'm going to break through to him.<br>I can't do this.<br>I let hope in.<br>I'm losing hope.<br>I'm strong and vulnerable.<br>I'm insecure and scared.<br>I want to see him.<br>I need space.<br><br>PICK SOMETHING! Match your words to your actions! Don't say one thing, do another and then complain about not knowing what's going on. It was one facepalm after another.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413195ra/813211.gif" width="500" height="201" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, I will say, that I do enjoy a good cocky asshole. They get my blood flowing, but there were times in the beginning where Colton came off a bit swarmy and creepy in his arrogance and pursuit of Rylee. He would tip to the wrong side of the scale for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410144855ra/11067084.gif" width="500" height="247" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>HOWEVER, I did enjoy the lighter side of their banter. I enjoyed Colton opening up to Rylee, even if it was by accident. Seeing how easily she could draw out that side of him, really drew me in. Those moments where he showed his vulnerability is what kept me going. And Rylee did have times of rational thought, even if they were fleeting.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414467041ra/11657942.gif" width="500" height="297" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One place where these two got along REALLY well was in the sex department. That had me paying close attention. Their chemistry was... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383495949ra/6578728.gif" width="350" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I may not have been wow'd with this first book and spent most of the time being wishy-washy with the characters, but I liked it enough to want to know where this is going. To know what's lurking in Colton's past. What skeletons are in his closet. And that ending had me reaching for the second book faster than I would have thought when I started. <br><br><i>**There's one small writing-style distraction that I'd like to point out. There was an OVER-ABUNDANCE of the use of the word "for" instead of "because." I'm really hoping that's remedied in the second book. It drove me batty! For example (and I'm just making up a sentence), instead of saying "I wanted to understand him because he was a mystery to me," the author would write "I wanted to understand him for he was a mystery to me." That's too formal for my liking. And sentences like that are used ALL. THE. TIME. Maybe it's just me, but the tone comes off pompous. I normally wouldn't mention something like this, but it's used so much that it became a distraction.</i><br><br>Now I'm off to see where all of this is going to go. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414467041ra/11657943.gif" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1456334962822808601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2683051579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683051579" />
    <a title="Melissasfandomworld" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34871171-melissasfandomworld"><img alt="Melissasfandomworld" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486125037p2/34871171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683051579?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissasfandomworld" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissasfandomworld" href="/user/show/34871171-melissasfandomworld">Melissasfandomworld</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/30164950-driven">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683051579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4358663436734810385">Ok, so this was a difficult review to write. I don't like to put a negative vibe on a review, you know? And it's sometimes hard to find the right words when describing what you didn't like about a book. I always want to highlight the things I did like as well, but mostly this is a book I just couldn't fall in love with and I feel very sad about that because I had high hopes for it!<br/><br/>I wanted to read this book because it was on my kindle, the synopsis sounds great and I know that Passionflix even t</span>
  <span id="freeText4358663436734810385" style="display:none">Ok, so this was a difficult review to write. I don't like to put a negative vibe on a review, you know? And it's sometimes hard to find the right words when describing what you didn't like about a book. I always want to highlight the things I did like as well, but mostly this is a book I just couldn't fall in love with and I feel very sad about that because I had high hopes for it!<br><br>I wanted to read this book because it was on my kindle, the synopsis sounds great and I know that Passionflix even turned it into a movie. So I was quite intrigued and felt like reading it all of a sudden, so I started reading it. And even though it wasn't to my liking, I still felt like reviewing it and sharing my review so here we go!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/my-thoughts-1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947476._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="669" height="148" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><em>The start of the books is quite unbelievable already I think. She sees him making out with someone in a dark corner, finds herself then trapped in a closet and starts having a panic attack. He then 'rescues' her and out of the frigging blue they start making out, like wtf. And the moment when she recognizes him as the man who was busy with another woman a minute ago, she still lets herself loose on him. Like WTF.. &lt; I'm all for insta-lust and sometimes also act on it fast, but the situation has to be right for it, and this situation didn't feel right to me personally. </em><br><br>The story-line was okay-ish I guess, but there wasn't really a lot of refreshment present. I did like some elements like the minor characters and the social work elements added into the story. Those were very interesting to read about. So the details of the characters work, the settings etc were different but other than that, there were quite a lot of similarities with the 50 shades of Grey books for example. Quite a lot indeed...<br><br>Our male lead for example, is almost exactly like Christian Grey but with another name: Colton Donovan. He's troubled by his past, he 'can't' love someone as he so clearly states at some point, he doesn't want children and doesn't do relationships in a traditional way.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <p>
    <em>
      <strong>“You know that deep down, a tiny part of that proper, respectable woman you are, wants to visit that reckless, sexy, uninhibited place inside you that’s begging to get out. A place I can undoubtedly help you find.”</strong>
    </em>
  </p>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>I so so sooo wanted to love this character because his intensity was quite mesmerizing and I liked the goodness he had in him as well as the sexy mystery surrounding him. I could forgive him for some of his actions because of the things that happened to him in the past - <em>that we barely get information about so it's a lot of guessing</em> -. We know he's traumatized because of his early childhood but my sympathy only goes So far, especially when there's barely any elaboration as to What happened to him - <em>I guess the author's saving this for the sequel since it ends on a Cliffhanger as well</em>. There wasn't any refreshing quality to his character in the end and that was quite a shame I guess.<br><br>One moment our female lead is a strong character who defends herself at times, but in the moments she needs to step up her game, she doesn't. I was so frustrated with her throughout the entire book. I'm not one to speak up for myself or who easily confronts people, but this character was the cherry to the cake. I wanted to shake her so badly sometimes. There was just no way I could get a good feel for her. I could say she acts this way because of his behavior towards her, which is partly true I guess, but for the most part I think this character was just all over the place and gave me a whiplash with how often she changed her mind about things from one second to the next.<br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <p>
    <em>
      <strong>“He is my fire on a cold night, the sun warming my skin on a cool spring morning, the wind caressing my face on an autumn day—he is everything that makes me feel alive, and whole, and beautiful.”</strong>
    </em>
  </p>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>So yeah, because of the extremely amount of back and forths between these two characters, the romance wasn't always quite believable to me. It's obvious he has feelings for her and he'll probably takes his time recognizing them for what they are - Hello Christian! - and act upon them after making some stupid mistakes, but I don't know. I couldn't really get myself to care for it all unfortunately.<br><br>The chemistry and sexy times between these two characters though, was quite well written and enthralling to read, so there's that haha!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/conclusion.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947477.jpg" alt="" width="280" height="96" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book was just not for me I guess. I normally really like books like these, with such intense characters and an intense romance but this book.. The writing.. It was ALL over the place. The characters gave me whiplash, both of them. One moment, they're all lovey-dovey, the next they're not. One moment they're head strong and determined and within a span of only seconds, they completely turn around and decide to act completely different. It was frustrating and agitating to me.<br><br><em>And I'm one of those readers out there who really loved the 50 shades books when I first read them so many years ago - yeah, so shoot me, lol. And sure, there's a lot to say about the books and I know a lot of people don't like them but to me they're guilty pleasure.</em><br><br>So normally I wouldn't mind reading a book that has similarities with the 50 shades books - <em>and I guess that alone can be a turnoff for lots of people for example</em> - but I thought the execution of this book was just lacking? There definitely was potential here, but it unfortunately didn't turn for the better the more I read of it.<br><br>And even though I find the execution of this book lacking, it was still a fast-paced read to me. That's so funny though, because I more often than not didn't really like the characters and the execution of this entire story, but I couldn't stop reading either, lol.<br><br>So I finished the <em>book, which ends in a Cliffhanger which I foresaw seeing it has A lot of similarities to 50 shades, lol</em> - because I wanted to see the entire picture and see if I was missing something here and if maybe the book would turn into something better, but to me it ends here. I won't be reading its sequel.<br><br>I personally don't understand why so many people are so in love with this book but it was originally published in 2013 and that was right in the middle of the 50 shades HYPE so maybe that's why a lot of people started loving on this book back then? And of course, everyone's entitled to have their own opinions and feelings about a book so seeing I didn't love it, definitely doesn't mean someone else can't love it. If you like this synopsis and a story that has similarities to 50 shades, this may be a book you'd end up enjoying!<br><br>Thanks for reading!<br><br><a href="https://melissasfandomworld.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/melissa.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548010443i/26947478._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="590" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4358663436734810385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_606310203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606310203" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6049062-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460575899p2/6049062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606310203?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/6049062-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=kindle-own">kindle-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=new-adult-romance">new-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6049062-jen?shelf=march-reads">march-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606310203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10784267594482085717">This was a so-so book for me. I can't say that I loved it; but I certainly enjoyed parts of it. The sex scenes were written superbly, and the chemistry between Colton and Rylee was off the charts. As far as Ms. Bromberg's writing skills went, I thought she did a wonderful job, although I did have a few complaints with the story and how it resembled parts of other popular books. I counted at least three other stories that had come out more than a year ago, that had very similar ideas displayed as</span>
  <span id="freeText10784267594482085717" style="display:none">This was a so-so book for me. I can't say that I loved it; but I certainly enjoyed parts of it. The sex scenes were written superbly, and the chemistry between Colton and Rylee was off the charts. As far as Ms. Bromberg's writing skills went, I thought she did a wonderful job, although I did have a few complaints with the story and how it resembled parts of other popular books. I counted at least three other stories that had come out more than a year ago, that had very similar ideas displayed as Driven. An example would have been Rylee and Colton sharing their feelings through sending one another songs to each other. I had read that idea in a book last year, and so I felt that it didn't hold the same meaning for me in this book.<br />One of the other major complaints I had was with Colton himself. I found him to be to full of himself, and quite frankly he seemed like a jerk in the beginning of this story. He redeemed himself a bit in my eyes while he interacted with some of the troubled boys that Rylee took care of through her job. Little Zander; who is traumatized and hadn't spoken in well over a year, happened to respond amazingly to Colton. For that alone, he melted my heart!<br /><br />I am very glad I waited to begin this series until books two and three were out! There is a cliffy at the end of Driven; but I am happy to report I can dive right in to Fueled!! I am going to follow my GR friends advice and continue on, and hopefully the books will get better as I go along!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10784267594482085717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606146859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18404473844336465803"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390966738i/8307525._SX540_.jpg' width='125' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>♥♥♥ 3.75 "MIXED SIGNALS" STARS ♥♥♥</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394082334ra/8805861.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After reading a few mixed reviews, I wasn't to sure if I wanted to read this one or not. In the end, I decided to try it for myself and hope for the best. After a weird start to the book--which already had me thinking I might not end up liking it--I became quite hooked. And was pleasantly surprised to end up enjoying this book.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br/><br/>"Let’s face it, you’re not a spend the night kind of guy, and I’m not a one-night </b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18404473844336465803" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390966738i/8307525._SX540_.jpg" width="125" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>♥♥♥ 3.75 "MIXED SIGNALS" STARS ♥♥♥</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394082334ra/8805861.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After reading a few mixed reviews, I wasn't to sure if I wanted to read this one or not. In the end, I decided to try it for myself and hope for the best. After a weird start to the book--which already had me thinking I might not end up liking it--I became quite hooked. And was pleasantly surprised to end up enjoying this book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"Let’s face it, you’re not a spend the night kind of guy, and I’m not a one-night stand kind of girl."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book begins with Rylee Thomas catching the famous racecar driver Colton Donovan in the act. However, she doesn't know it's him. She thinks he is just a random guy. This later leads her to become trapped in a storage closet where Colton rescues her from. And just like that, they get all hot and heavy with each other, making out like a couple of horny teens. You can see why I thought this book would not be for me. I mean she doesn't realize it at the time--since she didn't see his face--but he was just finished doing the deed with another woman and then starts making out with her. When she hears the familiar "Sweet Jesus" groan come out of him, she knows he's THE guy she just saw and pushes him away. So, the start wasn't too great to me, but I still continued. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394081806i/8805803._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Rylee was a twenty six year old independent woman. She works with an organization that helps orphaned children. She was kind, smart, and also quite feisty. But she also has some things she needs to move on from. She's attracted to Colton but knows that he is a big ol' man whore so she tries to stay away from him. She is confused by Colton's hot and cold attitude towards her. She thinks he only wants her because he thinks she is a challenge. He warns her about himself yet keeps telling her he wants to have her. Even I was getting severe whiplash.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394081806i/8805804._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Colton Donovan is a hot, arrogant, confident, dominant womanizer. He is relentless in his pursuit of Rylee and she soon realizes that there is more to him than what he projects. He apprears all calm and collected in front of everyone, but he is actually quite unsure of himself. After getting flashes of vulnerability from him, she wants to get to know the real him, but Colton doesn't want that to happen. I didn't get why he kept shutting her out, it was very frustrating.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"I'm seeing the true Colton Donavan - the unmasked version with a vulnerability that makes me want to reach over and take the hurt that often flickers through those green eyes and make it better. To show him that love and commitment are possible without complications. That it is real and pure and much more powerful than ever imagined with it is built and shared between two people."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>Rylee doesn't know what to do. Her friend's advice on moving on and living her life, with Colton's persistence causes her to finally give in to the sexual chemistry between them. At this point, I couldn't stop reading. I enjoyed the carefree banter between Rylee and Colton. As the story went on, we got to know a bit about Colton but there is still so much more to find out about him that he keeps hidden. We get to know a lot about Rylee and an event that occured that was a tough thing to go through. This is why Rylee was so hesitant to start anything with Colton. But I did get confused when after rejecting him, she didn't want him to leave. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>“He is my fire on a cold night, the sun warming my skin on a cool spring morning, the wind caressing my face on an autumn day—he is everything that makes me feel alive, and whole, and beautiful. And desired.” <br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>There were a few moments that were quite slow. Some things became to repetitive with "will we, won't we" thing going on. It just dragged on a bit too much for me in those moments. But there were also some angsty and intenst moments that had me not wanting to stop reading. The overall structure of this book is similar to the many books out there that involve a dominant millionaire. I didn't mind it so much because the stories weren't exactly the same. But still some might find they don't like the similarites of it, which is why I'm letting you know about it. I can understand that this might be the reason many people didn't like or didn't finish the book. There was one part where Rylee mentions Ana and Christian Grey. I kinda wish that wasn't in there since I really hate comparing books. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"You'll think you can change him and his ways. And just when that happens, you'll be over quicker than that last lap he just took."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383042211ra/6350905.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Overall, I enjoyed the Rylee, even if she confused me at times. I liked Colton despite being mercurial, he was hot and I loved that he had moments that showed his soft side. The sexual in this book was high, as was the steam. I also want to mention that I didn't find any of the sex scenes to have Bdsm in them. The story started a bit slow for me, and had a few slow moments throughout, but it did get better for me. I enjoyed the book and after the cliffhanger ending, I need to find out what happens next. I'm so happy I don't have to wait for the next book to come out!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18404473844336465803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_605962461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605962461" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz"><img alt="Elizabeth (Liz)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551206872p2/5495317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605962461?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Liz)" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz">Elizabeth (Liz)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ebook-read">ebook-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=contemporary-romance-read">contemporary-romance-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=arc-from-author-read">arc-from-author-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605962461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5502229784373808454">K. Bromberg, after a bit of a rough start, I have to admit that you’ve made a believer out of me. Do you think we can arrange for Mr. Colton Donovan to be taken on a test drive by yours truly?!<br/><br/>The rough start. Let’s get this out of the way. I was not a fan of the beginning of this story. Very early on, Driven seemed to be falling into the same trap many of the stories classified as erotic romance do. Rylee and Colton met for the first time, neither knowing who the other was, and immediately fell</span>
  <span id="freeText5502229784373808454" style="display:none">K. Bromberg, after a bit of a rough start, I have to admit that you’ve made a believer out of me. Do you think we can arrange for Mr. Colton Donovan to be taken on a test drive by yours truly?!<br /><br />The rough start. Let’s get this out of the way. I was not a fan of the beginning of this story. Very early on, Driven seemed to be falling into the same trap many of the stories classified as erotic romance do. Rylee and Colton met for the first time, neither knowing who the other was, and immediately fell into a passionate, sexual encounter. Granted, it was interrupted, but still. Then, naturally, there was a bachelorette auction where Rylee had to fill in, and, of course, Colton purchased a date with her. Bickering and banter ensued. The worst for me, though, was that Colton was coming off entirely smarmy and cheesy. I regret to say, at that moment, I thought the very worst of my hunk of racecar-drivin’ hottie. Very sad. <br /><br />Now, because I’m honest to a fault, I have to say that there were two small details pulled directly from the famous forerunners of the Millionaire-playboy Erotic Romance sub-genre. At first, this really bothered me. Detail one, flirty emails exchanged between Rylee and Colton. Detail two, the fact that Rylee called Colton ‘Ace’. I do believe there was a hint that ‘Ace’ may mean something specific to Rylee, so…I gave in on that. Also, I give K. Bromberg BIG props. She did include a shout-out to Christian and Ana, as well, so…yeah. I got past these two things…eventually *wink*.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Do you want to talk about it?” I ask softly, afraid to pry but wanting him to share what deep, dark secret has a hold on him. Me playing Ana to his Christian.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I will freely confess to the fact that I am a hard sell anymore on erotic romance (yes, I do have a point here, so hush and keep reading). It just feels like…been there, done that. I’m over it. Or, I thought I was. There are a select few authors who seem to be slowly resuscitating my long-dead obsession with this genre, and I’m thrilled to say that K. Bromberg has been added to that list!! How did she get there, you wonder, based on my review thus far? Well, this was only the first chapter, people! There was a heck of a lot more book to go, and I am so glad I kept reading!! <br /><br />So, FINALLY, what made me a believer? The story, my friends, the story. The further I got into the story, the more involved I became. Rylee worked for a company that had, basically, corporatized the foster care system. They had set up actual homes for children in need, and all employees would take shifts, helping to care for and counsel the children. I found the idea fascinating, and it was not simply used as a backdrop. It’s an important part of the story. I have no idea if it actually exists outside of this story or not. I could genuinely feel Rylee’s love and affection for these children, her worry and concern. I grew to love Rylee…and her best friend Haddie! These two were a lot of fun together…<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“My inner slut,” I reiterate, nodding my head, “I like that, but I think she’s lost.” “Oh, we can find her, sister!” she snickers. “She’s probably hiding behind the layers of cobwebs covering your crotch.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />All of this builds depth to a story. This is exactly what too many stories are missing these days, no matter the genre. Colton soon became involved with the company Rylee worked for in his capacity as a wealthy business owner, as well as racecar driver. He may have used some Alpha-male, rich-dude manipulation to make it happen, but, once it did, he was all-in. This is where my love (and lust) for Colton began to truly form. Big, tough man + kids in need = melty sighs of pure happiness. Colton’s baggage was heavy throughout this story. I could feel it weighing him down, just as I could feel Rylee’s past hanging heavy on her (and what a tragedy she was dealing with…it had me in tears to hear her describe it). We find out almost no details about Colton, but, thankfully, there are another two books on the way *grin*. <br /><br />Driven, as you can tell, really does have a great storyline. So, perfection for me is combining that great storyline with combustible chemistry and some *fanning self* very hot, but thankfully not kinky (I’m sooo over the kink right now), sex! Oh, yeah, baby. I needed a glass or ten of ice water to get through this one!! Let me just tell you all, as a public service, Colton Donovan in his driver jumpsuit?! You will have a…moment. Holy hot racecar driver, Batman!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“So, Ace,” I wriggle my eyebrows, “You looked kind of hot in your race suit!”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>I tilt my head and purse my lips as I study him back. “I wanted…” my voice is quiet, unsure, when I speak. The small smile playing at the corners of Colton’s lips gives me the surge of confidence I need to continue. Knowing he wants me. Knowing that he desires me and wants more of whatever this is, emboldens me. Empowers me to finish my thought. “I wanted you to take me right there on the hood of your car.”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />Truthfully, I couldn’t be happier with how Driven turned around so quickly for me. I ended up thoroughly enjoying the story, the characters, the chemistry AND the emotion-driven sex!! Many of you have probably already read and loved this fantastic first book in The Driven Trilogy. If you have, be sure to leave a review wherever you made your purchase, and remember to recommend the book to a friend. If you haven’t yet had the opportunity to enjoy the lovely, intelligent and compassionate Rylee Thomas OR one hellishly hot speedracer named Colton Donovan, GET THEE TO AN ONLINE BOOKSELLER NOW!! Book two can’t come soon enough for me!<br /><br /><br />**ARC provided by the author in exchange for an honest review**<br /><br /><br /><b>For more reviews, please visit <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a> or visit us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></b>.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r60xSdALhgCgO2cI7b+sfKH8rAA+YMX1uPDVaq/RuFmmmcZXP//vz6OEYVuFjqHg0haU9ESL/hnBlJOPsDdBMQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e4qaV9bXkfFiJAdioxH7ZQL0MPxSnqeNsmZD2NA26V1yvm1JOSP4PmGbATHLIPb5cR4ICCh1nGHLAgU9z9AQNQ==')})
  }
//]]>

With her MBA newly in hand, she has her future figured out --move up at the nightclub she works at and stay away from any guy who might trigger her obsessive love disorder. A perfect plan. But what Alayna didn\'t figure on is Hudson Pierce, the new owner of the nightclub. He\'s smart, rich, and gorgeous --the kind of guy Alayna knows to stay away from if she wants to keep her past tendencies in check.\n\nExcept, Hudson\'s fixed his sights on her. He wants her in his bed and makes no secret of it. Avoiding him isn\'t an option after he offers a business proposition she can\'t turn down and she\'s drawn further into his universe, unable to resist his gravitational pull.\n\nWhen she learns Hudson has a dark history of his own, she realizes too late that she\'s fallen for the worst man she could possibly get involved with. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2076626337259788824"><b><i>New York Times</i> Bestselling author K. Bromberg writes contemporary novels that contain a mixture of sweet, emotional, a whole lot of sexy, and a little bit of real. She likes to write strong heroines, and damaged heroes who we love to hate but can’t help to love.<br/><br/>A mom of three, she plots her novels in between school runs and soccer practices, more often than not with her laptop in tow.<br/><br/>Since publish</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2076626337259788824" style="display:none"><b><i>New York Times</i> Bestselling author K. Bromberg writes contemporary novels that contain a mixture of sweet, emotional, a whole lot of sexy, and a little bit of real. She likes to write strong heroines, and damaged heroes who we love to hate but can’t help to love.<br /><br />A mom of three, she plots her novels in between school runs and soccer practices, more often than not with her laptop in tow.<br /><br />Since publishing her first book on a whim in 2013, Kristy has sold over one and a half million copies of her books across sixteen different countries and has landed on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal Bestsellers lists over thirty times. Her Driven trilogy (Driven, Fueled, and Crashed) is currently being adapted for film by Passionflix with the first movie, Driven, releasing August 10th.<br /><br />With her imagination always in overdrive, she is currently scheming, plotting, and swooning over her latest hero. You can find out more about him or chat with Kristy on any of her social media accounts.
